It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:description": "Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:title": "Authors Guide"\n+  "keywords": "Plone, Documentation, SEO, meta, presentation, exercises, solutions, spellcheck, linkcheck, lexer"\n+---\n+\n+(authors-guide-label)=\n+\n+# Authors Guide\n+\n+This guide is for authors of Plone Documentation.\n+It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors.\n+For general markup syntax, see {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+\n+\n+(authors-html-meta-data-label)=\n+\n+## HTML and Open Graph Metadata\n+\n+All documents must have an `html_meta` directive at the top of every page.\n+When rendered to HTML, it inserts `<meta>` tags for improved search engine results and nicer social media posts.\n+Authors should include at least `description`, `property=og:description`, `property=og:title`, and `keywords` meta tags.\n+\n+The following is an example of `html_meta`.\n+Note that the content of the two tags `description` and `property=og:description` should be identical.\n+\n+```md\n+---\n+html_meta:\n+  "description": "Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:description": "Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:title": "Authors Guide"\n+  "keywords": "Plone, Documentation, SEO, meta, spellcheck, linkcheck, lexer"\n+---\n+```\n+\n+This renders in the HTML `<head>` section as follows.\n+\n+```html\n+<meta content="Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors." name="description" />\n+<meta content="Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors." property="og:description" />\n+<meta content="Authors Guide" property="og:title" />\n+<meta content="Plone, Documentation, SEO, meta, spellcheck, linkcheck, lexer" name="keywords" />\n+```\n+\n+Additional {term}`Open Graph` metadata is implemented through the Sphinx extension [`sphinxext-opengraph`](https://github.com/wpilibsuite/sphinxext-opengraph) and the [MyST `html_meta` directive](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html#setting-html-metadata), which resolves to the [Docutils `meta` directive](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#metadata).\n+See the site-wide configuration in {file}`conf.py`.\n+\n+\n+(authors-quality-checks-label)=\n+\n+## Quality checks\n+\n+We strive for high quality documentation, setting the following minimum standards.\n+\n+\n+(authors-markup-syntax-label)=\n+\n+### Markup syntax must be valid\n+\n+See both the specific markup syntax above and general markup in {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+\n+To validate markup, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/html/index.html` in a web browser.\n+\n+\n+(authors-english-label)=\n+\n+### American English Spelling, Grammar, and Syntax\n+\n+Spellings are enforced through [`spellcheck`](https://sphinxcontrib-spelling.readthedocs.io/en/latest/index.html).\n+We use the locale `en_US`.\n+\n+Spelling is configured in {file}`Makefile`, {file}`docs/conf.py`, and {file}`docs/spelling_wordlist.txt`.\n+\n+Authors should add new words and proper names using correct casing to {file}`docs/spelling_wordlist.txt`, sorted alphabetically.\n+\n+See [default settings and configuration options](https://sphinxcontrib-spelling.readthedocs.io/en/latest/customize.html).\n+\n+To validate spelling, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make spellcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/spellcheck/` for each training\'s misspellings.\n+\n+Because it is difficult to automate good English grammar and syntax, we do not strictly enforce it.\n+We also understand that contributors might not be fluent in English.\n+We encourage contributors to make a reasonable effort, and to seek help from community members who are fluent in English.\n+When you submit a pull request, please select a Reviewer to review your work.\n+\n+\n+(authors-linkcheck-label)=\n+\n+### All links must be valid\n+\n+```{important}\n+Before you add a link, consider whether you really need it for the documentation.\n+Avoid linking to blog posts because they rapidly succumb to bitrot.\n+It is preferred to copy the content from the source and add a link to the source as a reference through a `seealso` admonition or footnote, than to merely link to the source.\n+```\n+\n+Valid links are enforced automatically through Sphinx\'s `linkcheck` builder.\n+\n+[Configuration of the `linkcheck` builder](https://www.sphinx-doc.org/en/master/usage/configuration.html#options-for-the-linkcheck-builder) is in {file}`Makefile` and {file}`docs/conf.py`.\n+\n+`linkcheck_ignore` supports regular expression syntax.\n+\n+When authors add a link to the documentation, it must be a valid public URL without requiring authentication.\n+\n+If it is not a valid link, or is private or local, then you must exclude it from `linkcheck` by wrapping it in single backticks.\n+\n+```md\n+Visit the URL `http://www.example.com` for an example.\n+```\n+\n+This will render as follows.\n+\n+> Visit the URL `http://www.example.com` for an example.\n+\n+If a link has succumbed to bit rot, then try finding the most recently scraped version on the [Internet Archive Wayback Machine](https://web.archive.org/), and update the link.\n+\n+To validate links, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make linkcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/presentation/output.txt` for a list of broken links.\n+\n+```{danger}\n+Please do not abuse `linkcheck_ignore`.\n+\n+There is a special place in hell reserved for contributors who do not bother to update bad links, either dead ones or redirects, causing `linkcheck` to fail.\n+And there is a doubly punishing place for those who disable `linkcheck` because there are too many bad links.\n+\n+Please do not be "that person".\n+```\n+\n+\n+(authors-syntax-highlighting-label)=\n+\n+### Syntax highlighting\n+\n+Pygments provides syntax highlighting in Sphinx.\n+\n+When including code snippets, you should specify the language.\n+Authors must use a proper [Pygments lexer](https://pygments.org/docs/lexers/) and not generate warnings.\n+\n+The snippet must be valid syntax for the language you specify, else it will not be highlighted properly.\n+Avoid adding comments to code snippets, unless you use valid comment syntax for that language.\n+For example, JSON does not allow comments.\n+\n+Do not indicate elided or omitted code with ellipses (`...` or `\xe2\x80\xa6`).\n+These are almost never valid syntax and will cause syntax highlighting to fail for the code block.\n+\n+\n+#### Choosing a Lexer\n+\n+Some lexers are less than perfect.\n+If your code block does not highlight well, then consider specifying a less ambitious lexer, such as `text`.\n+\n+Use `shell` for commands to be issued in a terminal session.\n+Do not include shell prompts.\n+This will make commands easy to copy and paste for readers.\n+\n+Use `console` for output of a shell session.\n+If you have a mix of a shell command and its output, then use `console`.\n+\n+If `xml` does not work well, then try `html`.\n+\n+`jsx` has a complex syntax that is difficult to parse.\n+We have high hopes for the project [`jsx-lexer`](https://github.com/fcurella/jsx-lexer).\n+We include it in our `requirements.txt` file.\n+Please contribute to its further development.\n+\n+The lexers `html+ng2`, `scss`, `http`, `less` are also suboptimal and particular.\n+\n+If no other lexer works well, then fall back to `text`.\n+At least then the build will succeed without warnings, although syntax highlighting for such snippets will not appear.\n+\n+\n+#### Validate the Lexer\n+\n+Always build the page to validate syntax.\n+The change should not be merged if there are any Sphinx warnings.\n+The Sphinx console will display any warnings, such as the following.\n+\n+```console\n+/Plone/documentation/classic-ui/bodyclasses.md:10: WARNING: Could not lex literal_block as "python". Highlighting skipped.\n+```\n+\n+The above warning indicates that the syntax is not valid.\n+Common mistakes include:\n+\n+- Using `...` or `\xe2\x80\xa6` to indicate omitted code.\n+  It is preferable to never use ellipses.\n+  If you must do that, comment it out using the language\'s comment syntax.\n+- Using comments in JSON.\n+- A previous code block bleeds through to the next due to invalid MyST syntax.\n+\n+To validate code block syntax, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html\n+```\n+\n+An [online demo of all lexers that Pygments supports](https://pygments.org/demo/) may be helpful to test out your code blocks and snippets for syntax highlighting.\n+You can also use the [`pygmentize`](https://pygments.org/docs/cmdline/) binary.\n+\n+When using the online lexer, if any red-bordered rectangles appear, then the lexer for Pygments interprets your snippet as not valid.\n+You can search the [Pygments issue tracker](https://github.com/pygments/pygments/search) for possible solutions, or submit a pull request to enhance the lexer.\n+\n+\n+## Synchronize the Browser While Editing\n+\n+Use gulp to view changes in the browser while editing documentation.\n+\n+Install the gulp command line utility.\n+\n+```shell\n+npm install --global gulp-cli\n+```\n+\n+Install the gulp project.\n+\n+```shell\n+npm install\n+```\n+\n+Run gulp while editing the training documentation.\n+\n+```shell\n+gulp\n+```\n+\n+Your system\'s default browser will launch and open a window http://localhost:3002/.\ndiff --git Documentation\n+\n+This document describes how to contribute to the Plone Documentation.\n+\n+Contributions to the Plone Documentation are welcome.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-permission-to-publish-label)=\n+\n+## Granting permission to publish\n+\n+Before you contribute, you must give permission to publish your contribution according to the license we use.\n+You may give that permission in two ways.\n+\n+- Sign the [Plone Contributor Agreement](https://plone.org/foundation/contributors-agreement).\n+  This method also covers contributions to Plone code.\n+  It is a one-time only process.\n+- In every pull request or commit message, include the following statement.\n+\n+  > I, [full name], agree to have this contribution published under Creative Commons 4.0 International License (CC BY 4.0), with attribution to the Plone Foundation.\n+\n+The Plone Documentation is licensed under the [Creative Commons Attribution 4.0 International License (CC BY 4.0)](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/).\n+A copy of the license is included in the root of this repository.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-manage-on-github-label)=\n+\n+## Managing contributions on GitHub\n+\n+Contributions are managed through the [Documentation repository on GitHub](https://github.com/plone/documentation).\n+\n+First discuss whether you should perform any work.\n+Any method below is acceptable, but are listed in order of most likely to get a response.\n+\n+- [Search for open issues](https://github.com/plone/documentation/issues) and comment on them.\n+- [Create a new issue](https://github.com/plone/documentation/issues/new/choose).\n+- Discuss during conferences, trainings, and other Plone events.\n+- Ask on the [Plone Community Forum, Documentation topic](https://community.plone.org/c/documentation/13).\n+- Ask in the [Plone chat on Discord](https://discord.com/invite/zFY3EBbjaj).\n+\n+As a convenience, at the top right of every page, there is a GitHub navigation menu.\n+Tap, click, or hover over the GitHub Octocat icon for options.\n+\n+```{image} _static/github-navigation.png\n+:alt: GitHub navigation menu \n+```\n+\n+You can use this menu to quickly navigate to the source repository, open an issue, or suggest an edit to the current document.\n+Of course, you can use whichever tools you like.\n+\n+Next edit files, commit your changes, push them to the remote repository, and submit a pull request to resolve the issue.\n+\n+Members who subscribe to the repository will receive a notification and review your request.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-roles-label)=\n+\n+## Contributor Roles\n+\n+Contributors to the Plone Documentation may perform one or many roles.\n+\n+- **Plone users and developers** use this documentation because it is accurate and actively maintained.\n+  People in these roles typically contribute minor corrections.\n+  They should read {doc}`setup-build` and {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+- **Authors** create Plone Documentation.\n+  They should read {doc}`setup-build` and {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+  They should also read {doc}`authors` for guidance and tips for writing good technical documentation.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-quality-requirements-label)=\n+\n+## Documentation quality requirements\n+\n+We use GitHub Actions with every pull request to enforce Training documentation quality.\n+We recommend that you build the documentation locally to catch errors and warnings early on.\n+See {doc}`setup-build` for instructions for how to set up and build the documentation and to run quality checks.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-code-of-conduct-label)=\n+\n+## Code of Conduct\n+\n+The Plone Foundation has published a [Code of Conduct](https://plone.org/foundation/materials/foundation-resolutions/code-of-conduct).\n+All contributors to the Plone Documentation follow the Code of Conduct.\n+\n+\n+```{toctree}\n+---\n+caption: Contributing\n+maxdepth: 2\n+hidden: true\n+---\n+\n+setup-build\n+writing-docs-guide\n+authors\n+```\ndiff --git spelling.\n+\n+**macOS**\n+\n+```shell\n+brew install enchant\n+```\n+\n+**Ubuntu**\n+\n+```shell\n+sudo apt-get install enchant\n+```\n+\n+Clone the Plone Documentation repository, then create and activate a virtual environment, and install project dependencies.\n+\n+```shell\n+git clone https://github.com/plone/documentation.git\n+cd documentation\n+python -m venv .\n+source bin/activate\n+pip install -r requirements.txt\n+```\n+\n+\n+(setup-build-available-documentation-builds-label)=\n+\n+## Available documentation builds\n+\n+All build and check documentation commands use the file `Makefile`.\n+\n+To see all available builds:\n+\n+```shell\n+make\n+```\n+\n+\n+### `html`\n+\n+`html` is the long narrative version used for the online documentation and by the trainer.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/html/index.html` in a web browser.\n+\n+\n+(setup-build-make-presentation-label)=\n+\n+### `presentation`\n+\n+`presentation` is an abbreviated version of the documentation.\n+It is designed for projectors which are typically low resolution and have limited screen space.\n+Trainers may present this version using a projector during a training.\n+\n+```shell\n+make presentation\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/presentation/index.html` in a web browser.\n+\n+Authors should read {ref}`authors-presentation-markup-label` for how to write markup for the presentation build.\n+\n+\n+### `linkcheck`\n+\n+`linkcheck` checks all links.\n+See {ref}`authors-linkcheck-label` for configuration.\n+\n+```shell\n+make linkcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/presentation/output.txt` for a list of broken links.\n+\n+\n+### `spellcheck`\n+\n+`spellcheck` checks the spelling of words.\n+See {ref}`authors-english-label` for configuration.\n+\n+```shell\n+make spellcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/spellcheck/` for each training\'s misspellings.\n+\n+\n+### `html_meta`\n+\n+`html_meta` adds a meta data section to each chapter if missing.\n+See {ref}`authors-html-meta-data-label` for more info.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html_meta\n+```\ndiff --git a/docs/contributing/writing-docs-guide.md "description": "General Guide to Writing Documentation"\n+  "keywords": "Documentation, Plone, Sphinx, MyST, reStructuredText, Markdown"\n+---\n+\n+# General Guide to Writing Documentation\n+\n+This guide provides general help for writing documentation for Plone Trainings.\n+\n+\n+## MyST, reStructuredText, and Markdown\n+\n+We use [MyST, or Markedly Structured Text](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/), a rich and extensible flavor of Markdown, for authoring training documentation.\n+\n+MyST extends {term}`Markdown` by incorporating all the features of {term}`reStructuredText` and {term}`Sphinx` and its extensions.\n+Contributors are welcome to use either Markdown or MyST syntax.\n+\n+MyST may be more familiar to reStructuredText authors.\n+MyST allows the use of a {term}`fence` and `{rst-eval}` to evaluate native reStructuredText.\n+This may be useful when Markdown does not provide sufficient flexibility, such as for `figure`.\n+\n+\n+### MyST Syntax Reference\n+\n+The following are frequently used snippets and examples.\n+\n+```{seealso}\n+\n+**Official MyST documentation**\n+\n+- [The MyST Syntax Guide](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html)\n+- [MyST Syntax Reference](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/reference.html)\n+```\n+\n+\n+#### Targets and Cross-Referencing\n+\n+```{seealso}\n+[The MyST Syntax Guide > Targets and Cross-Referencing](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html#targets-and-cross-referencing)\n+```\n+\n+##### Link to a Chapter or Page\n+\n+```md\n+We created an add-on in the last chapter {doc}`/mastering-plone/volto_custom_addon`.\n+```\n+\n+We created an add-on in the last chapter {doc}`/mastering-plone/volto_custom_addon`.\n+\n+\n+(writing-docs-guide-link-heading-label)=\n+\n+##### Link to a Heading\n+\n+```md\n+(writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label)=\n+\n+###### Hello Heading\n+\n+Read the section {ref}`writing-docs-guide-link-heading-label`.\n+```\n+\n+(writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label)=\n+\n+###### Hello Heading\n+\n+Read the section {ref}`writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label`.\n+\n+\n+##### Link to an Arbitrary Location\n+\n+```md\n+(example-target-label)=\n+\n+I have an HTML anchor above me.\n+\n+Click the link to visit {ref}`my text <example-target-label>`.\n+```\n+\n+(example-target-label)=\n+\n+I have an HTML anchor above me.\n+\n+Click the link to visit {ref}`my text <example-target-label>`.\n+\n+\n+##### Link to External Page\n+\n+```md\n+Use [Shimmer](http://example.com) for cleaner whiter teeth.\n+```\n+\n+Use [Shimmer](http://example.com) for cleaner whiter teeth.\n+\n+\n+##### Images and Figures\n+\n+[Figures](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#figure) allow a caption and legend, whereas [images](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#images) do not.\n+\n+Use `image` for anything but diagrams.\n+\n+Use `figure` for diagrams.\n+\n+Images and figures should always include `alt` text.\n+\n+From [Web Accessibility In Mind (WebAIM)](https://webaim.org/techniques/alttext/):\n+\n+> Alternative text serves several functions:\n+> - It is read by screen readers in place of images allowing the content and function of the image to be accessible to those with visual or certain cognitive disabilities.\n+> - It is displayed in place of the image in browsers if the image file is not loaded or when the user has chosen not to view images.\n+> - It provides a semantic meaning and description to images which can be read by search engines or be used to later determine the content of the image from page context alone.\n+\n+Accessibility is part of the [Plone brand and identity](https://plone.org/accessibility).\n+\n+````md\n+```{image} /_static/standards.png\n+:alt: XKCD "Standards" comic strip\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```{image} /_static/standards.png\n+:alt: XKCD "Standards" comic strip\n+```\n+\n+````md\n+```{eval-rst}\n+.. figure:: /_static/voting_flowchart.png\n+    :alt: Voting flowchart\n+\n+    This is a caption in a single paragraph.\n+    \n+    This is a legend, which consists of all elements after the caption.\n+    It can include a table.\n+    \n+    ======  =======\n+    Symbol  Meaning\n+    ======  =======\n+    \xe2\x83\x9e       Object\n+    \xe2\xac\xad       View\n+    \xe2\x9e\x9e       Flow\n+    ======  =======\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```{eval-rst}\n+.. figure:: /_static/voting_flowchart.png\n+    :alt: Voting flowchart\n+\n+    This is a caption in a single paragraph.\n+    \n+    This is a legend, which consists of all elements after the caption.\n+    It can include a table.\n+    \n+    ======  =======\n+    Symbol  Meaning\n+    ======  =======\n+    \xe2\x83\x9e       Object\n+    \xe2\xac\xad       View\n+    \xe2\x9e\x9e       Flow\n+    ======  =======\n+```\n+\n+\n+##### Code Block\n+\n+A Python code snippet without reStructuredText options, using a simple fence.\n+\n+````md\n+```python\n+a = 2\n+print("my 1st line")\n+print(f"my {a}nd line")\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```python\n+a = 2\n+print("my 1st line")\n+print(f"my {a}nd line")\n+```\n+\n+A Python code snippet with reStructuredText options, using a fence with the parsed reStructuredText directive `code-block`.\n+\n+````md\n+```{code-block} python\n+:linenos:\n+:emphasize-lines: 1, 3\n+\n+a = 2\n+print("my 1st line")\n+print(f"my {a}nd line")\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```{code-block} python\n+:linenos:\n+:emphasize-lines: 1, 3\n+\n+a = 2\n+print("my 1st line")\n+print(f"my {a}nd line")\n+```\n+\n+##### Escape literal backticks inline\n+\n+```md\n+This is MyST syntax for term ``{term}`React` ``\n+```\n+\n+This is MyST syntax for term ``{term}`React` ``\n+\n+\n+\n+##### Glossary terms\n+\n+Add a term to the {ref}`glossary-label`, located at {file}`/glossary.md`.\n+\n+```md\n+React\n+    [React](https://reactjs.org/) is a JavaScript library for building user interfaces.\n+    Volto, the frontend for Plone 6, uses React.\n+```\n+\n+Reference a term in the {ref}`glossary-label`.\n+\n+```md\n+Using {term}`React` makes frontends fun again!\n+```\n+\n+Using {term}`React` makes frontends fun again!\n+\n+\n+\n+## Abridged Plone Documentation Styleguide\n+\n+Guides should be informational, but friendly.\n+\n+Address the reader by using "you" instead of "the user".\n+\n+Avoid contractions, and spell out the words.\n+For example, use "do not" instead of "don\'t".\n+\n+Please do not follow PEP8 maximum line length standard.\n+Documentation is narrative text and images, not Python code.\n+\n+Use one sentence per line.\n+Keep sentences short and understandable.\n+This will greatly improve the editing and maintenance of your documentation.\n+\n+\n+## General Documentation Writing References\n+\n+- [Write the Docs - Documentation Guide](https://www.writethedocs.org/guide/)\n+- [A Guide to Em Dashes, En Dashes, and Hyphens](https://www.merriam-webster.com/words-at-play/em-dash-en-dash-how-to-use)\n+\n+\n+### English grammar, spelling, punctuation, and syntax\n+\n+Because it is difficult to automate good English grammar and syntax, we do not strictly enforce it.\n+We also understand that contributors might not be fluent in English.\n+We encourage contributors to make a reasonable effort, and to seek help from community members who are fluent in English.\n+Please ask!\ndiff --git a/docs/glossary.md b/docs/glossary.md\nnew file mode 100644\nindex 00000000..29e909cc\n--- /dev/null\n+++ b/docs/glossary.md\n@@ [Linode.com](https://www.linode.com/) is an American privately owned virtual private server provider company based in Galloway, New Jersey, United States.\n+\n+DigitalOcean\n+    [DigitalOcean, distributed continuous integration service used to build and test software projects hosted at GitHub.\n+    Open source projects may be tested with limited runs via [travis-ci.org](https://travis-ci.org).\n+\n+Solr\n+    [Solr](https://solr.apache.org/) is a popular, blazing-fast, open source enterprise search platform built on Apache Lucene.\n+\n+ZCML\n+    The [Zope Configuration Mark-up Language](https://docs.plone.org/develop/addons/components/zcml.html).\n+\n+Diazo\n+    [Diazo theme engine guide](https://docs.diazo.org/en/latest/).\n+    Diazo allows you to apply a theme contained in a static HTML web page to a dynamic website created using any server-side technology.\n+\n+Dexterity\n+    [Dexterity](https://github.com/plone/plone.dexterity), the base framework for building content types, both through-the-web and as filesystem code for Zope.\n+\n+Dublin Core\n+    The Dublin Core Schema is a small set of vocabulary terms that can be used to describe web resources (video, images, web pages, etc.), as well as physical resources such as books or CDs, and objects like artworks.\n+\n+ZMI\n+    The Zope Management Interface.\n+    The ZMI is a direct interface into the backend software stack of Plone.\n+    While it can still serve as a valuable tool for Plone specialists to fix problems or accomplish certain tasks, it is not recommended as searchtools.js\n+ * ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n+ *\n+ * Sphinx JavaScript utilities for the full-text search.\n+ *\n+ * :copyright: Copyright 2007-2021 by the Sphinx team, see AUTHORS.\n+ * :license: BSD, see each result\n+    // The function takes a result array [filename, title, anchor, descr, score]\n+    // and returns the new score.\n+    /*\n+    score: function(result) {\n+      return result[4];\n+    },\n+    */\n+\n+    // query matches the full name of an object\n+    objNameMatch: 11,\n+    // or matches in the last dotted part of the object name\n+    objPartialMatch: 6,\n+    // Additive scores depending on the priority of the object\n+    objPrio: {0:  15,   // used to be importantResults\n+              1:  5,   // used to be objectResults\n+              2: -5},  // used to be unimportantResults\n+    //  Used when the priority is not in the mapping.\n+    objPrioDefault: 0,\n+\n+    // query found in title\n+    title: 15,\n+    partialTitle: 7,\n+    // query found in terms\n+    term: 5,\n+    partialTerm: 2\n+  };\n+}\n+\n+if (!splitQuery) {\n+  function splitQuery(query) {\n+    return query.split(/\\s+/);\n+  }\n+}\n+\n+/**\n+ * Search Module\n+ */\n+var Search = {\n+\n+  _index : null,\n+  _queued_query : null,\n+  _pulse_status : -1,\n+\n+  htmlToText : function(htmlString) {\n+      var virtualDocument = document.implementation.createHTMLDocument(\'virtual\');\n+      var htmlElement = $(htmlString, virtualDocument);\n+      htmlElement.find(\'.headerlink\').remove();\n+      docContent = htmlElement.find(\'[role=main]\')[0];\n+      if(docContent === undefined) {\n+          console.warn("Content block not found. Sphinx search tries to obtain it " +\n+                       "via \'[role=main]\'. Could you check your theme or template.");\n+          return "";\n+      }\n+      return docContent.textContent || docContent.innerText;\n+  },\n+\n+  init : function() {\n+      var params =   if (params.doc_section) {\n+            var doc_section = params.doc_section[0];\n+            $(\'select[name="doc_section"]\')[0].value = doc_section;\n+          }\n+          this.performSearch(query, doc_section);\n+      }\n+  },\n+\n+  loadIndex : function(url) {\n+    $.ajax({type: "GET", url: url, data: null,\n+            dataType: "script", cache: true,\n+            complete: function(jqxhr, textstatus) {\n+              if (textstatus != "success") {\n+                document.getElementById("searchindexloader").src = url;\n+              }\n+            }});\n+  },\n+\n+  setIndex : function(index) {\n+    var q;\n+    this._index = index;\n+    if ((q = this._queued_query) !== null) {\n+      this._queued_query = null;\n+      Search.query(q);\n+    }\n+  },\n+\n+  hasIndex : function() {\n+      return this._index !== null;\n+  },\n+\n+  deferQuery : function(query) {\n+      this._queued_query = query;\n+  },\n+\n+  stopPulse : function() {\n+      this._pulse_status = 0;\n+  },\n+\n+  startPulse : function() {\n+    if (this._pulse_status >= 0)\n+        return;\n+    function pulse() {\n+      var i;\n+      Search._pulse_status = (Search._pulse_status + 1) % 4;\n+      var dotString = \'\';\n+      for (i = 0; i < Search._pulse_status; i++)\n+        dotString += \'.\';\n+      Search.dots.text(dotString);\n+      if (Search._pulse_status > -1)\n+        window.setTimeout(pulse, 500);\n+    }\n+    pulse();\n+  },\n+\n+  /**\n+   * perform a search for something (or wait until index is loaded)\n+   */\n+  performSearch : function(query, doc_section) {\n+    // create the required interface elements\n+    this.out = $(\'#search-results\');\n+    this.title = $(\'\').appendTo(this.out);\n+    this.dots = $(\'<span></span>\').appendTo(this.title);\n+    this.status = $(\'<p class="search-summary">&nbsp;</p>\').appendTo(this.out);\n+    this.output = $(\'<ul class="search"/>\').appendTo(this.out);\n+\n+   var i;\n+\n+    // stem the searchterms and add them to the correct list\n+    var stemmer = new Stemmer();\n+    var searchterms = [];\n+    var excluded = [];\n+    var hlterms = [];\n+    var tmp = splitQuery(query);\n+    var objectterms = [];\n+    for (i = 0; i < tmp.length; i++) {\n+      if (tmp[i] !== "") {\n+          objectterms.push(tmp[i].toLowerCase());\n+      }\n+\n+      if ($u.indexOf(stopwords, tmp[i].toLowerCase()) != -1 || tmp[i] === "") {\n+        // skip this "word"\n+        continue;\n+      }\n+      // stem the word\n+      var word = stemmer.stemWord(tmp[i].toLowerCase());\n+      // prevent stemmer from cutting word smaller than two chars\n+      if(word.length < 3 && tmp[i].length >= 3) {\n+        word = tmp[i];\n+      }\n+      var toAppend;\n+      // select the correct list\n+      if (word[0] == \'-\') {\n+        toAppend = excluded;\n+        word = word.substr(1);\n+      }\n+      else {\n+        toAppend = searchterms;\n+        hlterms.push(tmp[i].toLowerCase());\n+      }\n+      // only add if not already in the list\n+      if (!$u.contains(toAppend, word))\n+        toAppend.push(word);\n+    }\n+    var highlightstring = \'?highlight=\' + $.urlencode(hlterms.join(" "));\n+\n+    // console.debug(\'SEARCH: searching for:\');\n+    // console.info(\'required: \', searchterms);\n+    // console.info(\'excluded: \', excluded);\n+\n+    // prepare search\n+    var terms = this._index.terms;\n+    var titleterms = this._index.titleterms;\n+\n+    // array of [filename, title, anchor, }\n+\n+    // lookup as search terms in fulltext\n+    results = results.concat(this.performTermsSearch(searchterms, excluded, terms, titleterms));\n+\n+    // let the scorer override scores with a custom scoring function\n+    if (Scorer.score) {\n+      for (i = 0; i < results.length; i++)\n+        results[i][4] = Scorer.score(results[i]);\n+    }\n+\n+    // Filter results by doc_section\n+ })\n+    }\n+\n+    // Enrich item with parent doc_section title\n+    for (i = 0; i < results.length; i++) \n+      results[i][6] = results[i][6] || \'TODO Documentation title\';\n+\n+    // now sort the results by score (in opposite order of appearance, since the\n+    // display function below uses pop() to retrieve items) and then\n+    // alphabetically\n+    results.sort(function(a, b) {\n+      var left = a[4];\n+      var right = b[4];\n+      if (left > right) {\n+        return 1;\n+      } else if (left < right) {\n+        return -1;\n+      } else {\n+        // same score: sort        }\n+        listItem.append($(\'<a/>\').attr(\'href\',\n+            linkUrl +\n+            highlightstring + item[2]).html(item[1]));\n+        \n+        listItem.append($(\'<span class="title_doc_section">\' + item[6] + \'</span>\'));\n+\n+        if (item[3]) {\n+          listItem.append($(\'<span> (\' + item[3] + \')</span>\'));\n+          Search.output.append(listItem);\n+          setTimeout(function() {\n+            displayNextItem();\n+          }, 5);\n+        } else if (DOCUMENTATION_OPTIONS.HAS_SOURCE) {\n+          $.ajax({url: requestUrl,\n+                  dataType: "text",\n+                  complete: function(jqxhr, textstatus) {\n+                    var data = jqxhr.responseText;\n+                    if (data !== \'\' && data !== undefined) {\n+                      listItem.append(Search.makeSearchSummary(data, searchterms, hlterms));\n+                    }\n+                    Search.output.append(listItem);\n+                    setTimeout(function() {\n+                      displayNextItem();\n+                    }, 5);\n+                  }});\n+        } else {\n+          // no source available, just display title\n+          Search.output.append(listItem);\n+          setTimeout(function() {\n+            displayNextItem();\n+          }, 5);\n+        }\n+      }\n+      // search finished, update title and status message\n+      else {\n+        Search.stopPulse();\n+        Search.title.text(_(\'Search Results\'));\n+        if (!resultCount)\n+          Search.status.text(_(\'Your search did not match any documents. Please make sure that all words are spelled correctly and that you\\\'ve selected enough categories.\'));\n+        else\n+            Search.status.text(_(\'Search finished, found %s page(s) matching performObjectSearch : function(object, otherterms) {\n+    var filenames = this._index.filenames;\n+    var docnames = this._index.docnames;\n+    var objects = this._index.objects;\n+    var objnames = this._index.objnames;\n+    var titles = this._index.titles;\n+\n+    var i;\n+    var results = [];\n+\n+    for (var prefix in objects) {\n+      for (var name in objects[prefix]) {\n+        var parts = fullnameLower.split(\'.\');\n+          // check for different match types: exact matches of full name or\n+          // "last name" (i.e. last dotted part)\n+          if (fullnameLower == object || parts[parts.length - 1] == object) {\n+            score += Scorer.objNameMatch;\n+          // matches in last name\n+          } else if (parts[parts.length - 1].indexOf(object) > -1) {\n+            score += Scorer.objPartialMatch;\n+          }\n+          var match = objects[prefix][name];\n+          var objname = objnames[match[1]][2];\n+          var title = titles[match[0]];\n+          // If more than one term searched for, we require other words to be\n+          // found in the name/title/description\n+          if (otherterms.length > 0) {\n+            var haystack = (prefix + \' \' + name + \' \' +\n+                            objname + \' \' + title).toLowerCase();\n+            var allfound = true;\n+            for (i = 0; i < otherterms.length; i++) {\n+ continue;\n+            }\n+          }\n+          var descr = objname + _(\', in \') + title;\n+\n+          var anchor = match[3];\n+          if (anchor === \'\')\n+            anchor = fullname;\n+          else if (anchor == \'-\')\n+            anchor = objnames[match[1]][1] + \'-\' + fullname;\n+          // add custom score for some objects according to scorer\n+          if results.push([docnames[match[0]], fullname, \'#\'+anchor, descr, score, filenames[match[0]]]);\n+        }\n+      }\n+    }\n+\n+    return results;\n+  },\n+\n+  /**\n+   * See $& means the whole matched string\n+  },\n+\n+  /**\n+   * search for full-text terms in the index\n+   */\n+  performTermsSearch : function(searchterms, excluded, terms, titleterms) {\n+    var docnames = this._index.docnames;\n+    var filenames = this._index.filenames;\n+    var titles = this._index.titles;\n+\n+    var i, j, file;\n+    var fileMap = {};\n+    var scoreMap = {};\n+    var results = [];\n+\n+    // perform the search on the required terms\n+    for (i = 0; i < searchterms.length; i++) {\n+      var word = searchterms[i];\n+      var files = [];\n+      var _o = [\n+        {files: terms[word], score: Scorer.term},\n+        {files: titleterms[word], score: Scorer.title}\n+      ];\n+      // add support for partial matches\n+      if (word.length > 2) {\n+        var      }\n+        }\n+        for (var w in titleterms) {\n+          if (w.match(word_regex) && !titleterms[word]) {\n+              _o.push({files: titleterms[w], score: Scorer.partialTitle})\n+          }\n+        }\n+      }\n+\n+      // no match but word was a required one\n+      if ($u.every(_o, function(o){return o.files === undefined;})) {\n+        break;\n+      }\n+      // found _files[j];\n+          if (!(file in scoreMap))\n+            scoreMap[file] = {};\n+          scoreMap[file][word] = o.score;\n+        }\n+      });\n+\n+      // create the mapping\n+      for (j = 0; j < files.length; j++) {\n+        file = files[j];\n+        if (file in fileMap && fileMap[file].indexOf(word) === -1)\n+          fileMap[file].push(word);\n+        else\n+          fileMap[file] = [word];\n+      }\n+    }\n+\n+    // now check if the files don\'t contain excluded terms\n+    for (file in fileMap) {\n+      var valid = true;\n+\n+      // check if all requirements are matched\n+      var filteredTermCount = // as search terms with length < 3 are discarded: ignore\n+        searchterms.filter(function(term){return term.length > 2}).length\n+      if (\n+        fileMap[file].length != searchterms.length &&\n+        fileMap[file].length != filteredTermCount\n+      ) continue;\n+\n+      // ensure that none of the excluded terms is in the search result\n+      for (i = 0; i < excluded.length; i++) {\n+        if (terms[excluded[i]] == file ||\n+            titleterms[excluded[i]] == file ||\n+            $u.contains(terms[excluded[i]] || [], file) ||\n+            $u.contains(titleterms[excluded[i]] || [], file)) {\n+          valid = false;\n+          break;\n+        }\n+      }\n+\n+      // if we have still a valid result we can add it to the result list\n+      if (valid) {\n+        // select one (max) score for the file.\n+        // for better ranking, we should calculate ranking by using words statistics like basic tf-idf...\n+        var score = $u.max($u.map(fileMap[file], function(w){return scoreMap[file][w]}));\n+        function getParentTitle(f) {\n+          let parentdocname = docnames[f].split(\'/\')[0] + \'/index\';\n+          let parentID = docnames.indexOf(parentdocname);\n+          let title = parentID === -1 ? \'Plone Documentation\' : titles[parentID];\n+          return title\n+        }\n+        results.push([docnames[file], titles[file], \'\', null, score, filenames[file], getParentTitle(file)]);\n+      }\n+    }\n+    return results;\n+  },\n+\n+  /**\n+   * helper function to return class="context"></p>\').text(excerpt);\n+    $.each(hlwords, function() {\n+      rv = rv.highlightText(this, \'highlighted\');\n+    });\n+    return rv;\n+  }\n+};\n+\n+$(document).ready(function() It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:description": "Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors."\n+  "property=og:title": "Authors Guide"\n+  "keywords": "Plone, Documentation, SEO, meta, spellcheck, linkcheck, lexer"\n+---\n+```\n+\n+This renders in the HTML `<head>` section as follows.\n+\n+```html\n+<meta content="Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors." name="description" />\n+<meta content="Authors\' guide to writing Plone Documentation. It covers configuring quality checks and syntax for writing markup that is of particular interest to authors." property="og:description" />\n+<meta content="Authors Guide" property="og:title" />\n+<meta content="Plone, Documentation, SEO, meta, spellcheck, linkcheck, lexer" name="keywords" />\n+```\n+\n+Additional {term}`Open Graph` metadata is implemented through the Sphinx extension [`sphinxext-opengraph`](https://github.com/wpilibsuite/sphinxext-opengraph) and the [MyST `html_meta` directive](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html#setting-html-metadata), which resolves to the [Docutils `meta` directive](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#metadata).\n+See the site-wide configuration in {file}`conf.py`.\n+\n+\n+(authors-quality-checks-label)=\n+\n+## Quality checks\n+\n+We strive for high quality documentation, setting the following minimum standards.\n+\n+\n+(authors-markup-syntax-label)=\n+\n+### Markup syntax must be valid\n+\n+See both the specific markup syntax above and general markup in {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+\n+To validate markup, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/html/index.html` in a web browser.\n+\n+\n+(authors-english-label)=\n+\n+### American English Spelling, Grammar, and Syntax\n+\n+Spellings are enforced through [`spellcheck`](https://sphinxcontrib-spelling.readthedocs.io/en/latest/index.html).\n+We use the locale `en_US`.\n+\n+Spelling is configured in {file}`Makefile`, {file}`docs/conf.py`, and {file}`docs/spelling_wordlist.txt`.\n+\n+Authors should add new words and proper names using correct casing to {file}`docs/spelling_wordlist.txt`, sorted alphabetically.\n+\n+See [default settings and configuration options](https://sphinxcontrib-spelling.readthedocs.io/en/latest/customize.html).\n+\n+To validate spelling, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make spellcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/spellcheck/` for misspellings.\n+\n+Because it is difficult to automate good English grammar and syntax, we do not strictly enforce it.\n+We also understand that contributors might not be fluent in English.\n+We encourage contributors to make a reasonable effort, and to seek help from community members who are fluent in English.\n+When you submit a pull request, please select a Reviewer to review your work.\n+\n+\n+(authors-linkcheck-label)=\n+\n+### All links must be valid\n+\n+```{important}\n+Before you add a link, consider whether you really need it for the documentation.\n+Avoid linking to blog posts because they rapidly succumb to bitrot.\n+It is preferred to copy the content from the source and add a link to the source as a reference through a `seealso` admonition or footnote, than to merely link to the source.\n+```\n+\n+Valid links are enforced automatically through Sphinx\'s `linkcheck` builder.\n+\n+[Configuration of the `linkcheck` builder](https://www.sphinx-doc.org/en/master/usage/configuration.html#options-for-the-linkcheck-builder) is in {file}`Makefile` and {file}`docs/conf.py`.\n+\n+`linkcheck_ignore` supports regular expression syntax.\n+\n+When authors add a link to the documentation, it must be a valid public URL without requiring authentication.\n+\n+If it is not a valid link, or is private or local, then you must exclude it from `linkcheck` by wrapping it in single backticks.\n+\n+```md\n+Visit the URL `http://www.example.com` for an example.\n+```\n+\n+This will render as follows.\n+\n+> Visit the URL `http://www.example.com` for an example.\n+\n+If a link has succumbed to bit rot, then try finding the most recently scraped version on the [Internet Archive Wayback Machine](https://web.archive.org/), and update the link.\n+\n+To validate links, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make linkcheck\n+```\n+\n+Open `/_build/linkcheck/output.txt` for a list of broken links.\n+\n+```{danger}\n+Please do not abuse `linkcheck_ignore`.\n+\n+There is a special place in hell reserved for contributors who do not bother to update bad links, either dead ones or redirects, causing `linkcheck` to fail.\n+And there is a doubly punishing place for those who disable `linkcheck` because there are too many bad links.\n+\n+Please do not be "that person".\n+```\n+\n+\n+(authors-syntax-highlighting-label)=\n+\n+### Syntax highlighting\n+\n+Pygments provides syntax highlighting in Sphinx.\n+\n+When including code snippets, you should specify the language.\n+Authors must use a proper [Pygments lexer](https://pygments.org/docs/lexers/) and not generate warnings.\n+\n+The snippet must be valid syntax for the language you specify, else it will not be highlighted properly.\n+Avoid adding comments to code snippets, unless you use valid comment syntax for that language.\n+For example, JSON does not allow comments.\n+\n+Do not indicate elided or omitted code with ellipses (`...` or `\xe2\x80\xa6`).\n+These are almost never valid syntax and will cause syntax highlighting to fail for the code block.\n+\n+\n+#### Choosing a Lexer\n+\n+Some lexers are less than perfect.\n+If your code block does not highlight well, then consider specifying a less ambitious lexer, such as `text`.\n+\n+Use `shell` for commands to be issued in a terminal session.\n+Do not include shell prompts.\n+This will make commands easy to copy and paste for readers.\n+\n+Use `console` for output of a shell session.\n+If you have a mix of a shell command and its output, then use `console`.\n+\n+If `xml` does not work well, then try `html`.\n+\n+`jsx` has a complex syntax that is difficult to parse.\n+We have high hopes for the project [`jsx-lexer`](https://github.com/fcurella/jsx-lexer).\n+We include it in our `requirements.txt` file.\n+Please contribute to its further development.\n+\n+The lexers `html+ng2`, `scss`, `http`, `less` are also suboptimal and particular.\n+\n+If no other lexer works well, then fall back to `text`.\n+At least then the build will succeed without warnings, although syntax highlighting for such snippets will not appear.\n+\n+\n+#### Validate the Lexer\n+\n+Always build the page to validate syntax.\n+The change should not be merged if there are any Sphinx warnings.\n+The Sphinx console will display any warnings, such as the following.\n+\n+```console\n+/Plone/documentation/classic-ui/bodyclasses.md:10: WARNING: Could not lex literal_block as "python". Highlighting skipped.\n+```\n+\n+The above warning indicates that the syntax is not valid.\n+Common mistakes include:\n+\n+- Using `...` or `\xe2\x80\xa6` to indicate omitted code.\n+  It is preferable to never use ellipses.\n+  If you must do that, comment it out using the language\'s comment syntax.\n+- Using comments in JSON.\n+- A previous code block bleeds through to the next due to invalid MyST syntax.\n+\n+To validate code block syntax, run the following command.\n+\n+```shell\n+make html\n+```\n+\n+An [online demo of all lexers that Pygments supports](https://pygments.org/demo/) may be helpful to test out your code blocks and snippets for syntax highlighting.\n+You can also use the [`pygmentize`](https://pygments.org/docs/cmdline/) binary.\n+\n+When using the online lexer, if any red-bordered rectangles appear, then the lexer for Pygments interprets your snippet as not valid.\n+You can search the [Pygments issue tracker](https://github.com/pygments/pygments/search) for possible solutions, or submit a pull request to enhance the lexer.\n+\n+\n+## Synchronize the Browser While Editing\n+\n+Use `sphinx-autobuild` to view changes in the browser while editing documentation.\n+\n+```shell\n+make livehtml\n+```\n+\n+You can open a browser at http://127.0.0.1:8000/ to preview the covers contributions to Plone code.\n+  It is a one-time only process.\n+- In every pull request or commit message, include the following statement.\n+\n+  > I, [full name], agree to have this contribution published under Creative Commons 4.0 International License (CC BY 4.0), with attribution to the Plone Foundation.\n+\n+The Plone Documentation is licensed under the [Creative Commons repository.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-manage-on-github-label)=\n+\n+## Managing contributions on GitHub\n+\n+Contributions are managed through the [Documentation repository on GitHub](https://github.com/plone/documentation).\n+\n+First discuss whether you should perform any work.\n+Any method below is acceptable, but are listed in order of most likely to get a response.\n+\n+- [Search for open issues](https://github.com/plone/documentation/issues) and comment on them.\n+- [Create a new issue](https://github.com/plone/documentation/issues/new/choose).\n+- Discuss during conferences, trainings, and other Plone events.\n+- Ask on the [Plone Community Forum, Documentation topic](https://community.plone.org/c/documentation/13).\n+- Ask in the [Plone chat on Discord](https://discord.com/invite/zFY3EBbjaj).\n+\n+As a convenience, at the top right of every page, there is a GitHub navigation menu.\n+Tap, click, or hover over the GitHub Octocat icon for options.\n+\n+```{image} /_static/github-navigation.png\n+:alt: GitHub navigation menu \n+```\n+\n+You can use this menu to quickly navigate to the source repository, open an issue, or suggest an edit to the current document.\n+Of course, you can use whichever tools you like.\n+\n+Next edit files, commit your changes, push them to the remote repository, and submit a pull request to resolve the issue.\n+\n+Members who subscribe to the repository will receive a notification and review your request.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-roles-label)=\n+\n+## Contributor Roles\n+\n+Contributors to the Plone Documentation may perform one or many roles.\n+\n+- **Plone users and developers** use this documentation because it is accurate and actively maintained.\n+  People in these roles typically contribute minor corrections.\n+  They should read {doc}`setup-build` and {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+- **Authors** create Plone Documentation.\n+  They should read {doc}`setup-build` and {doc}`writing-docs-guide`.\n+  They should also read {doc}`authors` for guidance and tips for writing good technical documentation.\n+\n+\n+(contributing-quality-requirements-label)=\n+\n+## Documentation quality requirements\n+\n+We use GitHub Actions with every pull request to enforce Plone Documentation quality.\n+We recommend that you build the documentation locally to catch errors the Code of Conduct.\n+\n+\n+```{toctree}\n+---\n+caption: Contributing\n+maxdepth: 2\n+hidden: true\n+---\n+\n+setup-build\n+writing-docs-guide\n+authors\n+```\ndiff --git misspellings.\n+\n+\n+### `html_meta`\n+\n+`html_meta` adds a meta data section to each chapter if missing.\n+See {ref}`authors-html-meta-data-label` for more info.\n+\n+```shell\n+make reStructuredText, Markdown"\n+---\n+\n+# General Guide to Writing Documentation\n+\n+This guide provides general help for writing documentation for Plone.\n+\n+\n+## MyST, reStructuredText, and Markdown\n+\n+We use [MyST, or Markedly Structured Text](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/), a rich and extensible flavor of Markdown, for authoring training documentation.\n+\n+MyST extends {term}`Markdown` by incorporating all the features of {term}`reStructuredText` and {term}`Sphinx` and its extensions.\n+Contributors are welcome to use either Markdown or MyST syntax.\n+\n+MyST may be more familiar to reStructuredText authors.\n+MyST allows the use of a {term}`fence` and `{rst-eval}` to evaluate native reStructuredText.\n+This may be useful when Markdown does not provide sufficient flexibility, such as for `figure`.\n+\n+\n+### MyST Syntax Reference\n+\n+The following are frequently used snippets and examples.\n+\n+```{seealso}\n+\n+**Official MyST documentation**\n+\n+- [The MyST Syntax Guide](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html)\n+- [MyST Syntax Reference](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/reference.html)\n+```\n+\n+\n+#### Targets and Cross-Referencing\n+\n+```{seealso}\n+[The MyST Syntax Guide > Targets and Cross-Referencing](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/syntax/syntax.html#targets-and-cross-referencing)\n+```\n+\n+##### Link to a Chapter or Page\n+\n+```md\n+Here is how to set up and build the documentation locally {doc}`/contributing/setup-build`.\n+```\n+\n+Here is how to set up and build the documentation locally {doc}`/contributing/setup-build`.\n+\n+\n+(writing-docs-guide-link-heading-label)=\n+\n+##### Link to a Heading\n+\n+```md\n+(writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label)=\n+\n+###### Hello Heading\n+\n+Read the section {ref}`writing-docs-guide-link-heading-label`.\n+```\n+\n+(writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label)=\n+\n+###### Hello Heading\n+\n+Read the section {ref}`writing-docs-guide-hello-heading-label`.\n+\n+\n+##### Link to an Arbitrary Location\n+\n+```md\n+(example-target-label)=\n+\n+I have an HTML anchor above me.\n+\n+Click the link to visit {ref}`my text <example-target-label>`.\n+```\n+\n+(example-target-label)=\n+\n+I have an HTML anchor above me.\n+\n+Click the link to visit {ref}`my text <example-target-label>`.\n+\n+\n+##### Link to External Page\n+\n+```md\n+Use [Shimmer](http://example.com) for cleaner whiter teeth.\n+```\n+\n+Use [Shimmer](http://example.com) for cleaner whiter teeth.\n+\n+\n+##### Images and Figures\n+\n+[Figures](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#figure) allow a caption and legend, whereas [images](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/docs/ref/rst/directives.html#images) do not.\n+\n+Use `image` for anything but diagrams.\n+\n+Use `figure` for diagrams.\n+\n+Images and figures should always include `alt` text.\n+\n+From [Web Accessibility In Mind (WebAIM)](https://webaim.org/techniques/alttext/):\n+\n+> Alternative text serves several functions:\n+> - It is read by screen readers in place of images allowing the content and function of the image to be accessible to those with visual or certain cognitive disabilities.\n+> - It is displayed in place of the image in browsers if the image file is not loaded or when the user has chosen not to view images.\n+> - It provides a semantic meaning and description to images which can be read by search engines or be used to later determine the content of the image from page context alone.\n+\n+Accessibility is part of the [Plone brand and identity](https://plone.org/accessibility).\n+\n+````md\n+```{image} /_static/standards.png\n+:alt: XKCD "Standards" comic strip\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```{image} /_static/standards.png\n+:alt: XKCD "Standards" comic strip\n+```\n+\n+````md\n+```{eval-rst}\n+.. figure:: /_static/voting_flowchart.png\n+    :alt: Voting flowchart\n+\n+    This is a caption in a single paragraph.\n+    \n+    This is a legend, which consists of all elements after the caption.\n+    It can include a table.\n+    \n+    ======  =======\n+    Symbol  Meaning\n+    ======  =======\n+    \xe2\x83\x9e       Object\n+    \xe2\xac\xad       View\n+    \xe2\x9e\x9e       Flow\n+    ======  =======\n+```\n+````\n+\n+```{eval-rst}\n+.. figure:: /_static/voting_flowchart.png\n+    :alt: Voting flowchart\n+\n+    This is a caption in a single paragraph.\n+    \n+    This is a legend, which user".\n+\n+Avoid contractions, and spell out the words.\n+For example, use "do not" instead of "don\'t".\n+\n+Please do not follow PEP8 maximum line length standard.\n+Documentation is narrative text and images, not Python code.\n+\n+Use one sentence per line.\n+Keep sentences short and understandable.\n+This will greatly improve the editing and maintenance of your documentation.\n+\n+\n+## General Documentation Writing References\n+\n+- [Write the Docs - Documentation Guide](https://www.writethedocs.org/guide/)\n+- [A Guide to Em Dashes, En Dashes, and true\n+\n+AWS\n+    [Amazon Web Services](https://aws.amazon.com/) offers reliable, scalable, and inexpensive cloud computing services.\n+    Free to join, pay only for what you use.\n+\n+Linode\n+    [Linode.com](https://www.linode.com/) is an American privately owned virtual private server provider company based in Galloway, New Jersey, United States.\n+\n+DigitalOcean\n+    [DigitalOcean, Inc.](https://www.digitalocean.com/) is an American cloud infrastructure provider headquartered in New York City with data centers worldwide.\n+\n+ZODB\n+    [A native object database for Python](https://zodb.org/en/latest/).\n+\n+Barceloneta\n+    The default theme for Plone 5.\n+\n+CMS\n+    Content Management System\n+\n+CSS\n+    Cascading Style Sheets (CSS) is a stylesheet language used for describing the (most of the times visual) representation of web pages.\n+\n+Grunt\n+    The JavaScript Task Runner.\n+    Automates the creation and manipulation of static assets for the theme.\n+\n+Less\n+    A dynamic stylesheet language that can be compiled into {term}`CSS` (Cascading Style Sheets).\n+\n+NPM\n+    npm is a package manager for the JavaScript programming language.\n+    It is the default package manager for the JavaScript runtime environment Node.js.\n+    Also a registry of JavaScript packages, similar to PyPI.\n+\n+TTW\n+    Through-The-Web, changes in the browser.\n+\n+S3\n+    [Amazon Web Services S3](https://aws.amazon.com/s3/).\n+    Object storage built to store and retrieve any amount of data from anywhere.\n+\n+NFS\n+    [Network File System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Network_File_System).\n+\n+Amazon Opsworks\n+    [AWS OpsWorks](https://aws.amazon.com/opsworks/) is a configuration management service that uses Chef, an automation platform that treats server configurations as code.\n+\n+Ansible\n+    [Ansible](https://www.ansible.com/) is an open source automation platform.\n+    Ansible can help you with configuration management, application deployment, task automation.\n+\n+Archetypes\n+    The deprecated framework for building content types in Plone.\n+\n+Chef\n+    [A configuration management tool written in Ruby and Erlang](https://www.chef.io/products/chef-infra/).\n+\n+CloudFormation\n+    [AWS CloudFormation](https://aws.amazon.com/cloudformation/) gives developers and systems administrators an way to create and manage a collection of related AWS resources, provisioning and updating them in an orderly and predictable fashion.\n+\n+Travis CI\n+    Travis CI is a hosted, distributed continuous integration service used to build and test software projects hosted at GitHub.\n+    Open source projects may be tested with limited runs via [travis-ci.org](https://travis-ci.org).\n+\n+Solr\n+    [Solr](https://solr.apache.org/) is a popular, blazing-fast, open source enterprise search platform built on Apache Lucene.\n+\n+ZCML\n+    The [Zope Configuration Mark-up Language](https://docs.plone.org/develop/addons/components/zcml.html).\n+\n+Diazo\n+    [Diazo theme engine guide](https://docs.diazo.org/en/latest/).\n+    Diazo allows you to apply a theme contained in a static HTML web page to a dynamic website created using any server-side technology.\n+\n+Dexterity\n+    [Dexterity](https://github.com/plone/plone.dexterity), the base framework for building content types, both through-the-web and as filesystem code for Zope.\n+\n+Dublin Core\n+    The Dublin Core Schema is a small set of vocabulary terms that can be used to describe web resources (video, images, web pages, etc.), as well as physical resources such as books or CDs, and objects like artworks.\n+\n+ZMI\n+    The Zope Management Interface.\n+    The ZMI is a direct interface into the backend software stack of Plone.\n+    While it can still serve as a valuable tool for Plone specialists to fix problems or accomplish certain tasks, it is not recommended as a regular tool for Plone maintenance.\n+\n+TALES\n+    TAL Expression Syntax (TALES) expression, which by default expects a path.\n+    Python and string expressions are also allowed.\n+\n+XML\n+    The Extensible Markup Language.\n+\n+XSLT\n+    The Extensible Stylesheet Language Transformations.\n+    A language which defines elements to describe transformations to be applied on a document.\n+\n+XPath\n+    XPath (XML Path Language) is a query language for selecting nodes from an XML document.\n+\n+Rapido application\n+    It contains the features you implement.\n+    It is a folder containing templates, Python code, and YAML files.\n+\n+block\n+    Blocks display a chunk of HTML which can be inserted in your Plone pages.\n+\n+element\n+    Elements are the dynamic components of your blocks.\n+    They can be input fields, buttons, or computed HTML.\n+    They can also return JSON if you call them from a JavaScript app.\n+\n+record\n+    A Rapido app is able to store data as records.\n+    Records are basic dictionaries.\n+\n+Project (Volto)\n+    The product of running `create-volto-app`, a customizable instance of Volto.\n+\n+Add-on (Volto)\n+    A JavaScript package that integrates with Volto\'s configuration registry.\n+\n+Add-on configuration loader (Volto)\n+    A function with signature `config => config`.\n+\n+Configuration registry (Volto)\n+    A singleton object modeled using JavaScript modules, accessible from the Volto\n+    project using the `~/config` path.\n+\n+Shadowing (Volto)\n+    Webpack provides an "alias" mechanism, where the path for a module can be aliased to another module.\n+    By using this mechanism Volto enables customization (file overrides), similar to `z3c.jbot.`\n+\n+Razzle\n+    A tool that simplifies SPA and SSR configuration for React projects.\n+\n+Webpack\n+    A tool that loads and bundles code and web resources using loaders.\n+\n+Webpack entrypoint\n+    The main files generated by webpack as a result.\n+    They typically contain the application source code based on modules bundled together, but it can also include other resources, such as static resources.\n+    It can contain code to automatically trigger the load of other JavaScript code files called "chunks".\n+\n+Babel\n+    A JavaScript compiler that "transpiles" newer standards JavaScript to something that any browser can load.\n+\n+Express\n+    A JavaScript HTTP server with a simple API to build custom applications.\n+    Volto uses it as its server.\n+\n+Server-Side Rendering (SSR)\n+    When first loading any Plone page, users will get HTML markup that closely matches the final DOM structure of the React components used to render that page.\n+\n+Single Page Application (SPA)\n+    A type of JavaScript application that aims to provide a better user experience by avoiding unnecessary reloading of the browser page, instead using AJAX to load backend information.\n+\n+Hot Module Replacement (HMR)\n+    A development feature provided by Webpack that automatically reloads, in the browser, the JavaScript modules that have changed on disk.\n+\n+Yeoman\n+    A popular scaffolding tool similar to Plone\'s `mr.bob` or `ZopeSkel`.\n+\n+CommonJS\n+    A JavaScript package standard, the equivalent of a Python wheel or egg.\n+    Enables JavaScript modules.\n+\n+Transpilation\n+    The transformation of JavaScript code that uses advanced language features, unavailable for some browsers, to code rewritten to support them.\n+\n+ES6\n+    ECMAScript 6, a newer version of the JavaScript language.\n+\n+mrs-developer\n+    Also called "missdev", a tool similar to buildout\'s `mr.developer`.\n+    It automatically downloads and keeps up to date copies of software and add-ons under development based on definitions stored in `mrs.developer.json`.\n+    As a byproduct of its update operations, it also automatically adjusts `jsconfig.json`, which is used by Volto to configure webpack aliases.\n+\n+Yarn\n+    A popular JavaScript package manager similar to NPM.\n+\n+Hydration (SSR)\n+    After loading an HTML page generated with SSR in the browser, React can "populate" the existing DOM elements, recreate and attach their coresponding components.\n+\n+JSX\n+    A dialect of JavaScript that resembles XML, it is transpiled by Babel to JavaScript functions.\n+    React uses JSX as its component templating.\n+\n+Scoped packages\n+    Namespace for JavaScript packages, they provide a way to avoid naming conflicts for common package names.\n+\n+middleware (Redux)\n+    Custom wrappers for the Redux store dispatch methods. \n+    They allow customizing the behavior of the data flow inside the redux store.\n+\n+hooks (React)\n+    Hooks are a React API that allow function components to use React features such as lifecycle methods, states, and so on.\n+\n+hoisting (Yarn)\n+    An optimization provided by Yarn.\n+    By default JavaScript packages will directly include dependencies inside their local node_modules.\n+    By hoisting we\'re "lifting" these inner dependencies to the top level `node_modules` directory, and thus optimize the generated bundles.\n+    In case two dependencies have conflicting version dependencies of the same library, the hoisting will not be possible (for that conflicting dependency) and you\'ll see multiple instances of the same library in the bundle, or you\'ll see that the add-on receives its own `node_modules` folder.\n+\n+React\n+    [React](https://reactjs.org/) is a JavaScript library for building user interfaces.\n+    Volto, the frontend for Plone 6, uses React.\n+\n+Sphinx\n+    [Sphinx](https://www.sphinx-doc.org/en/master/) is a tool that makes it easy to create intelligent and beautiful documentation.\n+    It was originally created for Python documentation, and it has excellent facilities for the documentation of software projects in a range of languages.\n+    Sphinx uses {term}`reStructuredText` as its markup language, and many of its strengths come from the power and straightforwardness of reStructuredText and its parsing and translating suite, {term}`Docutils`.\n+\n+Docutils\n+    [Docutils](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/) is an open-source text processing system for processing plaintext documentation into useful formats, such as HTML, LaTeX, man-pages, OpenDocument, or XML.\n+    It includes {term}`reStructuredText`, the easy to read, easy to use, what-you-see-is-what-you-get plaintext markup language.\n+\n+reStructuredText\n+    [reStructuredText (rST)](https://docutils.sourceforge.io/rst.html) is an easy-to-read, what-you-see-is-what-you-get plaintext markup syntax and parser system.\n+    The Plone 6 Documentation was written in reStructuredText originally, then converted to {term}`MyST` in 2022.\n+\n+MyST\n+    [Markedly Structured Text (MyST)](https://myst-parser.readthedocs.io/en/latest/) is a rich and extensible flavor of Markdown, for authoring Plone Documentation.\n+\n+Markdown\n+    [Markdown](https://daringfireball.net/projects/markdown/) is a text-to-HTML conversion tool for web writers.\n+\n+fence\n+    A method to extend basic MyST syntax.\n+    You can define a directive with backticks (`` ` ``) followed by a reStructuredText directive in curly brackets (`{}`), and a matching number of closing backticks.\n+    You can also nest fences by increasing the number of backticks. \n+    \n+    `````md\n+    ````{warning}\n+    There be dragons!\n+    ```{important}\n+    Dragons have feelings, too!\n+    ```\n+    ````\n+    `````\n+    \n+    ````{warning}\n+    There be dragons!\n+    ```{important}\n+    Dragons have feelings, too!\n+    ```\n+    ````\n+\n+Open Graph\n+    The [Open Graph protocol](https://ogp.me/) enables any web page to become a rich object in a social graph.\n+    For instance, this is used on Facebook to allow any web page to have the
